# Prospect Research — Cincinnati Market
## Ops for Shops — Initial Outreach List
### Compiled 2026-02-11

---

## How to Use This Document

This is your research dossier. The CSV (`prospect-list.csv`) is your working tracker. This document has the full context you need to write personalized outreach for each prospect.

For each prospect, the "Why They're a Good Prospect" and "Pain Point Signals" sections give you the specific observations that should drive your outreach message.

---

# ACCOUNTING FIRMS

## Priority 1 (Strongest Pain Signals)

### Flagel Huber Flagel (FHF)
- **Website:** https://fhf-cpa.com/
- **Size:** ~50 employees, 30+ CPAs
- **Founded:** 1933
- **Key People:** Randy Kuvin (former Managing Partner, stepped down 2023); Kevin Behrle (likely current leadership)
- **Tech Stack:** Offers IT services as a service line. No specific software advertised.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Glassdoor review explicitly states: **"The firm is behind in the times, trying to catch up but essentially dust in the wind."**
  - "Internal communication has been an issue"
  - "Work needs to be more evenly spread around to staff"
  - "Additional staffing is definitely necessary"
  - Hiring administrative staff for both Dayton and Cincinnati offices
  - Managing Partner transition (Kuvin stepped down 2023) — new leadership still finding footing
- **Why:** 90+ year old firm. Employees themselves are calling out the technology gap. Uneven workload distribution suggests workflow/process problems. Three office locations (Dayton, Cincinnati, Troy) mean coordination challenges. This is the strongest pain signal in the entire accounting list.

### Burke CPAs & Advisors
- **Website:** https://burkecpa.com/
- **Size:** ~33-47 employees, 18 CPAs, 3 partners
- **Founded:** 1984
- **Key People:** Patrick Burke (Managing Partner/Founder); Jake Burke (Partner, son); Pam Conner (Partner); Lauren (hired 2024 as Administrative Assistant for data entry, filing, electronic records)
- **Tech Stack:** No specific software mentioned publicly.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Glassdoor Cincinnati employees rate compensation 3.0/5: **"low, low pay for monotonous, grueling job"**
  - Work-life balance rated 3.5/5, career advancement 3.2/5
  - Only 55% of Cincinnati employees would recommend
  - Reviews mention "monotonous" work and employees leaving/being re-hired for better pay
  - Recently hired admin specifically for data entry and filing
  - Also hiring Accounting & Assurance Manager ($115K+)
- **Why:** Clear operational pain: manual data entry, filing, records management. Employee dissatisfaction with monotonous work = ripe for automation. Family-run firm where the founding partner may be open to modernizing. The admin hire signals they are trying to throw bodies at a process problem.

### Kirsch CPA Group
- **Website:** https://kirschcpa.com/
- **Size:** ~20-30 employees (ESOP, employee-owned since 2024)
- **Founded:** 1991
- **Key People:** Pete Abner (CEO, former partner, now leads post-ESOP); John Kirsch (Founder); Diane Glover (Director of Practice Growth — marketing, biz dev, recruiting)
- **Tech Stack:** QuickBooks Training & Consulting offered as a service line. Website mentions "strengthening traditional service offering with technology."
- **Pain Signals:**
  - ESOP transition in 2024 is a major organizational change — ownership transitions frequently trigger process/systems upheaval
  - Glassdoor (4.3/5) notes tax season stress
  - Actively hiring Tax Managers
  - Diane Glover's recruiting-focused role suggests talent acquisition is a pain point
- **Why:** Mid-transition firm. ESOP means new leadership (Pete Abner) is making decisions the founder previously made. Operational modernization is likely top of mind. Employee-owned firms have a financial incentive to improve efficiency.

## Priority 2

### Rudler, PSC
- **Website:** https://rudler.cpa/
- **Size:** ~58 employees + 7 remote (13% employee growth in 2024)
- **Founded:** ~1970s (50+ years)
- **Key People:** Alex Weidner (President); Tami Lawson (COO); Greg Lamping, David Neuhaus (Shareholders)
- **Tech Stack:** Rightworks AI, ChatGPT, Blue J for financial statement analysis. QuickBooks ProAdvisor. First firm of its size to go paperless. Cloud-first. Dedicated Technology Coordinator. Process Improvement Team (PIT) meets every 3 weeks. Won "2019 Best Accounting Firm for Technology."
- **Pain Signals:**
  - PIT team and Technology Coordinator = actively managing growing pains
  - 13% headcount growth in one year = onboarding and process scaling challenges
  - Hit $10M revenue milestone Dec 2024 — growth inflection points strain existing systems
  - Multiple offices expanding (Ft. Wright)
- **Why:** Most tech-savvy firm on the list — they already buy technology solutions. Rapid growth means budget and appetite. COO Tami Lawson is the operational decision maker. Approach from a "scale your processes" angle.

### Hebbeler & Weickert CPAs
- **Website:** https://hwcpa513.com/
- **Size:** ~5-10 employees
- **Founded:** 1984
- **Key People:** Robert Hebbeler (Co-Owner); Phillip Weickert (Co-Owner); Steven Goldman (Owner); **Erin Hart (Office Manager)**; Brandy Markley, Yassine Slimani (staff)
- **Tech Stack:** QuickBooks, Gusto (payroll partner), Microsoft 365
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Gusto payroll partner processing payroll for clients = integration friction with QuickBooks
  - Small team with identified Office Manager (Erin Hart) — likely overwhelmed juggling admin, client communication, ops
  - Multi-owner structure (3 owners) can create decision-making complexity
- **Why:** Known tech stack (QuickBooks + Gusto + M365) makes it easy to tailor a pitch. Gusto/QuickBooks integration pain is well-documented in the industry. Erin Hart is the "Backbone" persona from your voice doc.

## Priority 3

### Seibel & Katz CPAs
- **Website:** https://www.seibelkatzcpa.com/
- **Size:** ~6 employees
- **Key People:** Robert W. Seibel (Bob, President, MBA from Xavier, former controller for 12 years); John Rothgeb (Managing Partner)
- **Tech Stack:** QuickBooks (dedicated page). Serves healthcare, construction, restaurants, real estate.
- **Why:** Bob's controller background means he understands operations and systems — he'll "get" an efficiency pitch faster than a pure tax practitioner. Small enough that one conversation reaches the decision maker.

### Brauning & Company, LLC
- **Website:** https://www.brauningcpa.com/
- **Size:** ~5-10 employees
- **Key People:** Don Brauning (Owner)
- **Tech Stack:** QuickBooks (multiple website pages dedicated to it). Payroll, Part-Time CFO Services.
- **Why:** Single decision maker. QuickBooks-heavy practice with operational services (payroll, CFO, cash flow) = plenty of repetitive workflows. Relatively young firm (2012) in Blue Ash — likely more open to modern tools.

### Franz CPAs, Inc.
- **Website:** https://www.franzcpas.com/
- **Size:** ~9-10 employees
- **Key People:** Edward L. Soergel and Anthony J. Borgerding (Owners since Oct 2019, purchased from Timothy Franz)
- **Tech Stack:** Certified QuickBooks ProAdvisors. Serves clients in all 50 states from Cincinnati.
- **Why:** New ownership (2019) of an old firm (1967) = "inherited legacy systems" scenario. 10-person team serving 50 states = enormous coordination needs relative to headcount.

### Longschaefer & Company (LSC)
- **Website:** https://www.lsc.cpa/
- **Size:** ~18 employees
- **Key People:** Ronald A. Long (President/Co-Founder); Michael W. Long (Managing Partner); Ronald W. Schaefer (Partner/Co-Founder, 45 years experience)
- **Tech Stack:** AWS, Cloudflare CDN, WordPress, Microsoft 365
- **Why:** Succession planning likely on the horizon. Michael Long being groomed (Managing Partner while father is President). When firms plan succession, they need to systematize processes currently in partners' heads.

### Leverone & Associates
- **Website:** https://www.leveronecpa.com/
- **Size:** ~6-10 employees
- **Key People:** Francine Taggart (Owner/CPA)
- **Pain Signals:** Three offices with 6-10 employees = staff spread thin. Mixed reviews on accuracy suggest process/quality control gaps. $1.1M revenue with ~9 employees = tight margins.
- **Why:** Multi-location with tiny headcount = operational strain. Francine Taggart is likely both practitioner and ops person — she'd feel the pain most acutely.

### Atlas CPAs & Advisors PLLC
- **Website:** https://atlasfirms.com/
- **Size:** ~10-25 in Cincinnati (25 offices across 8 states)
- **Key People:** Loni Woodley (Managing Partner); Ben Holscher (Partner, promoted 2025)
- **Why:** Ben Holscher is a newly minted Cincinnati partner building his book — may welcome tools that help him scale.

### Disqualified Firms
- **Flynn & Company** — Merged into UHY (national) mid-2025
- **VonLehman CPA** — Merged with Dean Dorton Jan 2024 (~550 employees)
- **Cassady Schiller** — Acquired by KSM (Top 60 national) May 2024
- **Clark Schaefer Hackett** — 600+ employees, too large

# REAL ESTATE BROKERAGES

## Priority 1

### Comey & Shepherd Realtors
- **Website:** https://www.comey.com
- **Size:** ~180 agents, multiple offices
- **Founded:** 1946
- **Key People:** Scott Nelson (CEO since 1990); Terry Hankner (President, co-owner)
- **Tech Stack:** Microsoft IIS, Facebook Pixel, Google Remarketing, LeadingRE network. **No specific CRM or transaction management platform identified** — a potential gap.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Glassdoor (21 reviews): commission structure ~30% lower than industry average
  - Leadership communication described as "occasionally condescending"
  - Actively hiring: Office Administrator, Coordinator Assistant, Front Desk Receptionist
  - Moved/consolidated offices in 2025 (impacting ~40 employees) — cost management or restructuring
- **Why:** Large enough to have real operational pain, independent ownership means local decision-making, active admin hiring signals workflow gaps. The lack of identifiable modern CRM/transaction platform is a strong signal.

### RE/MAX Preferred Group (Locally Owned Franchise)
- **Website:** https://www.preferredgrouprealtors.com
- **Size:** ~150 agents, 10 offices
- **Founded:** 1998
- **Key People:** Chris Beresford (Co-Owner); Myles Beresford (Co-Owner)
- **Tech Stack:** BoldTrail (formerly kvCORE/Inside Real Estate). RE/MAX national tools, locally managed.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Agent review: **"The Bold Trail, when used properly, works"** — adoption/utilization of CRM is clearly an issue
  - 10 offices with ~15 agents each = multi-office management challenge
  - Local franchise owners make local decisions
- **Why:** Confirmed CRM adoption issues directly from an agent review. 10-office operation with multi-location complexity. Locally-owned.

### Cincy Flat Fee, LLC
- **Website:** https://cincyflatfee.com
- **Size:** ~5-10 agents
- **Key People:** Dan (Broker/Owner, UC Finance & Real Estate degree); Jen (likely co-owner); Julia Klaene (agent)
- **Tech Stack:** No CRM, transaction management, or tech tools publicly identified.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Flat-fee model ($1,500/transaction instead of 3%) = high volume essential to revenue
  - Every operational inefficiency directly impacts the bottom line
  - BBB A+ rating, 68 Birdeye reviews = active business but tiny team
  - Pricing tiers include full-service coordination (negotiations, inspections, document prep, closing) — all handled by small team
  - No visible tech stack + high-volume/low-margin model = classic recipe for manual process overload
- **Why:** Small team, high-volume model, thin margins, full-service commitment, and no visible tech. This brokerage likely has acute operational pain.

## Priority 2

### Team Herr / Private Real Estate Collection
- **Website:** https://teamherr.com
- **Size:** ~10-15 team members
- **Key People:** Heather Herr (CEO & Founder); Kelly (Ops Manager); Ann (Transaction Coordinator)
- **Tech Stack:** Claims "proprietary software platforms." No third-party CRM named.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Rapid growth: $15M to projected $100M in annual volume over four years
  - Multi-state (OH, KY, FL)
  - Invested in "robust back-office team infrastructure" in 2018 — hit a wall and had to rebuild ops
  - Dedicated ops manager and transaction coordinator = manual human roles doing heavy lifting
- **Why:** Named ops roles, multi-state complexity, tech-aware owner. "Proprietary platform" claim could be marketing language for a cobbled-together stack.

### Keynote Realtors
- **Website:** https://www.keynoterealtors.com
- **Size:** ~10-25 agents
- **Key People:** Nichell (Director of Marketing, named contact for agent recruitment)
- **Tech Stack:** **Nothing.** Only tech amenity listed: "Fast Roadrunner Internet Connections."
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Commission split starts 60/40, then 70/30 — not competitive in 2026
  - Also runs Keynote Realty Property Management (separate office, different phone number)
  - Zero observable tech stack = heavy reliance on manual processes
  - Separate property management operation = potentially fragmented ops between divisions
- **Why:** Classic small independent brokerage with minimal tech, property management side-business, and likely significant manual workflow pain.

### RE/MAX Victory + Affiliates
- **Website:** https://www.joinvictory.com
- **Size:** ~220 agents, 7 offices
- **Key People:** Tyler Morton (Broker/Owner, Ohio); Rod Fussinger, Kent Dailey, Jim Schack (Broker/Owners, Kentucky)
- **Pain Signals:**
  - 2020 merger of RE/MAX Victory and RE/MAX Affiliates = tech stack integration was a recent challenge
  - Split ownership (Morton = OH, Fussinger/Dailey/Schack = KY)
  - "Fastest growing REMAX in Southern Ohio and Northern Kentucky"
  - 220 agents across 7 offices = 30+ agents per office
- **Why:** Post-merger integration, multi-state ops with split ownership, rapid growth.

## Priority 3

### Plum Tree Realty
- **Website:** https://www.plumtreerealty.com
- **Size:** ~20-40+ agents
- **Key People:** Kevin Conley (EVP Sales)
- **Tech Stack:** kvCORE CRM (free to agents), Dotloop (free to agents). 100% commission model ($275/month flat fee).
- **Why:** Known tech stack. Thin-margin model may limit budget, but efficiency gains have outsized impact. Question is whether anyone is managing/configuring tools centrally.

### TREO Realtors
- **Website:** https://www.treorealtors.com
- **Size:** ~15-20 agents
- **Key People:** Brett Keppler (Broker/Owner, also founded Nekst — a task-management SaaS for real estate agents)
- **Tech Stack:** Dotloop, DocuSign, likely Nekst internally.
- **Why:** Tech-savvy owner who built a SaaS product out of his own brokerage pain. May self-solve, but excellent conversation partner and potential referral/network partner.

### Cutler Real Estate
- **Website:** https://www.cutlerhomes.com
- **Size:** ~100+ agents, 2 Cincinnati offices
- **Key People:** Andy Camp (Owner & President since 2017)
- **Tech Stack:** Delta Media Group platform. Tech-forward culture documented.
- **Why:** Tech-forward leadership is good for conversation. Cincinnati is their expansion market, potentially with less mature local ops.

### HUFF Realty
- **Website:** https://www.huff.com
- **Size:** ~100-200+ agents
- **Key People:** Susan Huff (Owner/Broker, 40 years as REALTOR)
- **Tech Stack:** In-house marketing/social media/tech team. Proprietary HUFF App. "Online business center." Berkshire Hathaway affiliate.
- **Why:** Has more resources but also more complexity. In-house tech team signals the BH-provided tools have gaps.

### Bonus: The Chabris Group / KW Seven Hills Realty
- **Website:** https://asktcg.com
- **Size:** 500+ clients/year. Top 10 brokerage by agent count.
- **Key People:** Peter Chabris (Team Leader and Broker/Owner)
- **Pain Signals:** Actively hiring transaction coordinators — job posting specifically mentions "completing and filing appropriate paperwork," "overseeing deadlines," "nurturing clients." KW Command platform + cold calling + door knocking.
- **Why:** 500+ annual transactions with active TC hiring = operation straining at the seams.

# LAW FIRMS

## Priority 1

### O'Connor, Acciani & Levy Co., LPA
- **Website:** https://www.oal-law.com/
- **Size:** ~13 attorneys, multiple offices (Downtown Cincinnati + Columbus + satellites in OH and NKY)
- **Practice Areas:** Personal Injury, Car Accidents, Medical Malpractice, Workers' Comp, Bankruptcy, Social Security Disability, Wrongful Death
- **Tech Stack:** CrazyEgg (heatmaps), Optimizely (A/B testing), ApexChat (live chat), Ngage Live, AppRiver (email security), McAfee SaaS Email, Google Analytics, Google Tag Manager. Sophisticated marketing tech, likely ahead of back-office.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Glassdoor 2.9/5 from 25 reviews
  - Indeed reviews: **"work environment is stressful due to constant competition"**
  - **"Workload for paralegals is entirely too much"**
  - **"Very high turnover"**
  - Multiple offices = coordination challenges
  - High-volume PI = massive caseload
- **Why:** Documented paralegal burnout and turnover. Marketing tech is sophisticated but back-office likely isn't. The paralegal workload complaint is the exact pain your automation services address.

### Barron Peck Bennie & Schlemmer Co., LPA
- **Website:** https://bpbslaw.com/
- **Size:** ~10 attorneys, 35 total employees
- **Founded:** 100+ years ago
- **Key People:** Michael S. Barron (Managing Partner, 16+ years in role); Daniel M. Bennie (Partner)
- **Practice Areas:** Estate Planning, Trust Admin, PI, Family Law/Divorce, Business Law, Employment, Commercial Real Estate, IP/Trademarks, Mediation, Probate, M&A
- **Pain Signals:**
  - **"Maintained its current size with the conscious goal of being able to retain a personalized approach"** — framing constraints as features
  - 12+ distinct practice areas across ~10 attorneys with 35 staff = complex, multi-workflow operations
  - Estate planning + real estate + M&A = extremely document-heavy
  - 2 offices (OH + KY)
- **Why:** 100+ year old firm. The "conscious choice to stay small" language often masks "we can't grow because our processes don't scale." Managing partner identified with 16+ years in role.

### Finney Law Firm, LLC
- **Website:** https://finneylawfirm.com/
- **Size:** 16 attorneys, 3 offices
- **Founded:** 2014
- **Key People:** Christopher P. Finney (Founder); Kevin J. Hopper (President)
- **Practice Areas:** Business Formation, Real Estate, Estate Planning, Commercial Litigation, Zoning/Land Use, 11+ other areas
- **Tech Stack:** States it "utilizes highly productive technology" but no specific platforms named.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - 16 attorneys across 3 offices in 14+ practice areas = operationally complex
  - Founded 2014 = relatively young, may not have mature tech stack
  - Real estate + business formation + estate planning = document-intensive
- **Why:** Tech-aspirational language means they're receptive. Young firm still building their stack. 3 offices + 14 practice areas = real complexity.

## Priority 2

### Musillo Unkenholt Immigration Law, LLC
- **Website:** https://www.muimmigration.com/
- **Size:** 10+ attorneys, 20-44 total staff
- **Key People:** Christopher T. Musillo (Managing Partner); Cindy J. Unkenholt (Co-Founding Partner)
- **Practice Areas:** Immigration Law (exclusively) — employment-based, family-based, healthcare, IT, construction, engineering, finance
- **Tech Stack:** Emphasizes "flat fees for services and superior case management." Likely uses specialized platforms (INSZoom, Docketwise, LawLogix).
- **Why:** Understands case management as competitive advantage. Serves multiple industries with different compliance requirements. Growth phase firms often hit scaling walls with initial tech choices.

### Bartlett & Weigle Co., L.P.A.
- **Website:** https://bartlettlaw.com/
- **Size:** 7 attorneys, 11 support staff (~18 total)
- **Founded:** 1981
- **Key People:** Douglas S. Weigle (Co-Founder); Bill Bartlett (Co-Founder)
- **Practice Areas:** Immigration, Criminal, Family Law, Estate Planning, Business Litigation, PI
- **Why:** Immigration + family + estate = multiple document-heavy practice areas with different workflow needs. 7 attorneys across 5+ practice areas with 11 staff = heavy admin burden per person.

### Freking Myers & Reul, LLC
- **Website:** https://www.fmr.law/
- **Size:** 12-14 attorneys, 3 offices (Cincinnati, Dayton, Denver)
- **Key People:** Kelly Mulloy Myers (Managing Partner)
- **Practice Areas:** Employment Law, PI, Education Law, Whistleblower/Qui Tam
- **Why:** Multi-state, multi-office. Employment law = extensive discovery. Was hiring Admin Assistant = operational growing pains. 300+ years combined experience may mean resistance to tech change.

### Treleven & Klingensmith, LLC
- **Website:** https://www.tkcincinnati.com/
- **Size:** ~6-8 attorneys, 3 locations
- **Key People:** John D. Treleven (Partner); Nicholas Klingensmith (Partner)
- **Practice Areas:** Divorce/Family Law, Estate Planning, PI, Criminal Defense, Business Consultation
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Formed from a **2020 merger** of Treleven Law LLC and Klingensmith Law LLC — mergers create system integration challenges
  - "Best law firm in Cincinnati" by CityBeat 5 years running, 4.9 stars (53 reviews) = high client volume
  - Squarespace website, no client portal
- **Why:** Merger integration may still be ongoing. High client volume with likely manual systems.

## Priority 3

### Schimpf, Ginocchio, Kehres & Clark
- **Website:** https://www.sgkclaw.com/
- **Size:** ~5 attorneys, 20+ total employees
- **Practice Areas:** Family Law, Estate Planning, PI, Business Law, Social Security Disability, Workers' Comp
- **Why:** 3:1 support-to-attorney ratio = heavy manual/admin work. Broad practice areas with small attorney team.

### Donnellon, Donnellon & Miller
- **Website:** https://donnellonlaw.com/
- **Size:** ~4 attorneys + support
- **Founded:** 1951
- **Key People:** Terrence M. Donnellon; Thomas E. Donnellon; R. Douglas Miller (Partners)
- **Why:** 75 years of accumulated processes. Separate court reporting and billing staff hints at siloed/disconnected tools.

### The Fleischer Law Firm LLC
- **Website:** https://www.immigrate2usa.com/
- **Size:** Small (2-3 attorneys)
- **Key People:** Neil Fleischer (Lead Attorney)
- **Practice Areas:** Immigration Law (exclusively since 1973)
- **Why:** 50+ years of accumulated case files. Immigration is the most document-intensive area of law.

### Ecosystem Note: SpliceNet Consulting
- **Website:** https://splice.net
- **Key People:** Jim Gast (Founder)
- **What:** Cincinnati-based MSP specializing in law firm IT. Supports Clio, Cosmolex, ActionStep, NetDocuments, iManage, Worldox, PCLaw, Amicus Attorney, Time Matters, HotDocs.
- **Why it matters:** Could be a referral partner or competitor depending on your offering. Worth knowing they exist.

# PROGRESSIVE NONPROFITS

## Priority 1

### Green Umbrella
- **Website:** https://greenumbrella.org
- **Size:** ~16 employees
- **Revenue:** ~$1.83M (FY 2024)
- **Key People:** Ryan Mooney-Bullock (Executive Director, $84,959 compensation)
- **Mission:** Regional sustainability alliance. Climate action, environmental justice, equitable access to green spaces.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Grew from 4 to 16 staff in a few years
  - Revenue from $720K to $2M
  - Operating at a deficit ($2.07M expenses vs $1.83M revenue)
  - Nearly half of expenses are salaries
  - 73.7% grant-dependent
  - Previously posted a Director of Finance role — professionalizing back-office
- **Why:** Squarely in the sweet spot. Rapid scaling (4x staff growth) almost certainly means they've outgrown their original donor management and volunteer tracking systems.

### Housing Opportunities Made Equal (HOME)
- **Website:** https://www.homecincy.org
- **Size:** 35 employees
- **Revenue:** ~$1.4M (FY 2024)
- **Key People:** Elisabeth Risch (ED); LaTonya Springs (Asst. Director); **Denese Benn (Director of Finance and Operations)**; Janet Brown (Director of Tenant Advocacy); Rebecca Griffin (Director of Education)
- **Mission:** Eliminating unlawful housing discrimination. Fair housing enforcement, Section 8 mobility, eviction prevention, mediation, education.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - 97% of revenue is grants — heavy grant management burden
  - 71% of expenses are salaries = very people-heavy operation
  - Spanish-language specialist + Testing and Investigations Coordinator = complex case management needs
  - Policy and Research Coordinator = data-intensive work
- **Why:** Right in the sweet spot. **Denese Benn (Director of Finance & Operations) is the perfect buyer.** She's the "Backbone" persona from your voice doc.

### Groundwork Ohio River Valley
- **Website:** https://www.groundworkorv.org
- **Size:** ~15 core staff + 165 seasonal youth employees
- **Revenue:** ~$2.48M (FY 2024, up 68% YoY)
- **Key People:** Sarah Kent (Executive Director)
- **Mission:** Environmental justice through youth workforce development. Employs 165+ young people annually.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - **68% revenue growth in a single year**
  - Managing 161 employees (mostly seasonal youth) with a ~$2.5M budget
  - Workforce onboarding, payroll, timekeeping, compliance for 300+ youth across multiple programs
  - Distributes grants to partner organizations ($279K in 2024) — grants on both receiving and giving side
  - EPA-funded programs require rigorous reporting
  - Founded only in 2019 — systems still being built
- **Why:** Explosive growth, complex workforce management, young organization with likely immature tech stack. The seasonal workforce management alone is a massive operational challenge.

### Ohio Justice & Policy Center (OJPC)
- **Website:** https://ohiojpc.org
- **Size:** ~25 employees, 2 offices (Cincinnati + Columbus)
- **Revenue:** ~$2M-$6M (growth trajectory)
- **Key People:** David Singleton (ED/President & CEO, but currently seeking replacement — leadership transition)
- **Mission:** Nonprofit law firm creating fair criminal justice systems through client-centered advocacy, policy reform, community education.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Rapid revenue growth ($2M to $6M)
  - Legal case management + policy advocacy + community education = multiple workstreams likely using different tools
  - Two offices require shared systems
  - **Currently seeking new President & CEO — leadership transition is when organizations re-evaluate infrastructure**
- **Why:** Growing fast, complex operations, leadership transition creates an opening for infrastructure conversations.

## Priority 2 (Strategic)

### Community Shares of Greater Cincinnati
- **Website:** https://cintishares.org
- **Size:** 4 employees
- **Revenue:** ~$299K (FY 2024)
- **Key People:** T. Duane Gordon (CEO)
- **Mission:** Federation of 31 progressive nonprofits + 14 Social Justice Incubator organizations. Federated fundraising. Fiscal sponsorship. Professional training.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - 4 people managing operations for a 45-org federation
  - Revenue declining (-4.1% YoY), expenses rising (+3.6%), assets dropping (-32.3%)
  - Fiscal sponsorship requires robust accounting and reporting
  - Federated fundraising means managing workplace giving campaigns across employers
- **Why:** Small as a direct client, but **STRATEGIC as a gateway to 45 progressive nonprofits in their network.** Solving their problems could create a pipeline to the entire Cincinnati progressive ecosystem.

### Women Helping Women
- **Website:** https://womenhelpingwomen.org
- **Size:** ~85 employees
- **Revenue:** ~$5.5M annual budget
- **Key People:** Kristin Shrimplin
- **Mission:** Preventing gender-based violence and empowering survivors. 24/7 hotline, hospital response across 25 hospitals, on-scene domestic violence response (DVERT), four counties.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Grew from 17 to 85 employees and $975K to $5.5M budget
  - 24/7 hotline + multi-county + 25 hospital partnerships = scheduling, case management, and donor system complexity
  - Organizations that grow this fast often carry legacy systems from their smaller days
- **Why:** Slightly above the sweet spot but the complexity and growth trajectory are compelling. Massive scaling likely means legacy systems.

### Over-the-Rhine Community Housing (OTRCH)
- **Website:** https://otrch.org
- **Size:** 56 employees
- **Revenue:** ~$13.8M (FY 2024, up 77% YoY)
- **Key People:** Mary Burke Rivers (Executive Director)
- **Mission:** Developing and managing 538 affordable housing units serving 980 residents.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - 77% revenue growth in one year
  - Property management + resident services + development pipeline = disconnected systems
  - Likely uses property management software (Yardi, AppFolio) plus separate fundraising/donor tools
- **Why:** Above revenue sweet spot but the complexity of combining housing management with social services creates significant operational needs.

## Priority 3

### Immigrant & Refugee Law Center (IRLC)
- **Website:** https://www.irlawcenter.org
- **Size:** 5 employees + 30 volunteers
- **Revenue:** ~$439K (FY 2022, likely growing)
- **Key People:** Mayra Casas Jackson (ED, took over from founder Julie Leftwich in 2024)
- **Mission:** Pro bono legal services for low-income immigrant and refugee families.
- **Why:** Recent leadership transition. Immigration law = meticulous case tracking. 30 volunteers need coordination. Slightly below revenue floor but growing.

### Ohio Organizing Collaborative (OOC)
- **Website:** https://www.ohorganizing.org
- **Size:** ~25 employees across Ohio
- **Key People:** Molly Shack (Executive Director)
- **Mission:** Statewide community organizing. 17 member organizations across major Ohio metros.
- **Tech Stack:** Action Network confirmed. Multi-city organizing needs shared CRM and campaign tracking.
- **Why:** Distributed team across 9 Ohio cities. ED job description specifically mentions **"oversight of all organizational support systems"** — they know they have infrastructure needs.

### Equality Ohio (Cincinnati hub)
- **Website:** https://www.equalityohio.org
- **Mission:** Statewide LGBTQ+ advocacy and legal aid.
- **Why:** Multi-city operations with Cincinnati presence. Legal clinics require case management. Worth investigating further.

### Greater Cincinnati Voter Collaborative (GCVC)
- **Website:** https://cincyvotes.org
- **Size:** Primarily volunteer-led, transitioning to paid staff
- **Mission:** Non-partisan civic engagement. Coalition of 54 organizations.
- **Why:** Low revenue prospect currently but **connector to 54 civic organizations.** Strategic value similar to Community Shares.

# MEDICAL / DENTAL PRACTICES

## Priority 1 (Strongest Pain Signals)

### Cincinnati Dental Services (CDS)
- **Website:** https://www.cincinnatidentalservices.com/
- **Size:** ~51-200 employees, 9 locations across SW Ohio and NKY
- **Founded:** ~1970s (50+ years)
- **Key People:** Kevin M. Lee, DDS (Ferguson/Eastgate); individual location teams with office-level managers (not publicly named)
- **Tech Stack:** Employee reviews note "the computer system is hard to learn." 9 separate office websites suggest fragmented digital presence.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - BBB: Patient **"charged $2,319 upfront for dentures"** and **"overcharged by $1,167"**
  - BBB: **"Calling the office numerous times to request explanations of charges with no one answering the phone or returning calls"**
  - BBB: Billing department **"changed their insurance coverage from one plan to another without notifying the customer"**
  - BBB: Patient **"called the billing office in December 2023, January 2024, and again in February 2024 regarding an overpayment but had not been refunded"**
  - BBB: **"The billing manager was not in (vacation, family emergency, etc.) and were promised callbacks that never came"**
  - Indeed: **"The computer system is hard to learn"**
- **Why:** 9 locations with fragmented billing systems, insurance coding errors, and chronic communication breakdowns. Patients calling 3+ months for refunds hitting voicemail. No centralized system connecting scheduling, billing, and patient communication.

### Kings Dental
- **Website:** https://www.kings.dental/
- **Size:** 19-27 employees, 2 locations, 4 doctors
- **Founded:** ~2021-2022 (3 years old, 11,000+ patients)
- **Key People:** Dr. Guy Gunacar (CEO/Owner); Mr. Ismail Gunacar (Co-Owner); Dr. Baljinder Singh; Dr. Sasha Hayes
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Glassdoor: **"Management is terrible, major drama, no organization, no training, and unprofessional environment"**
  - Glassdoor: **"Scheduling Coordinators have responsibilities that should be divided into four different positions"**
  - Glassdoor: **"They fire people and go through employees like water"**
  - Glassdoor: **"When employees think they're understanding the job, more work is added to their load"**
- **Why:** Fast-growing 3-year-old practice that has outgrown its operational foundation. Scheduling Coordinators doing the work of four people screams for workflow automation. Dr. Gunacar is the quintessential "Reluctant Operator" -- a dentist-turned-CEO scaling without infrastructure.

### The Urology Group
- **Website:** https://www.urologygroup.com/
- **Size:** 45+ physicians, 5+ locations

  - BBB: **"Abundant need to update and upgrade their medical records system -- clunky and unreliable"**
  - BBB: Patient **"billed multiple times for things they had already paid"**
  - BBB: Patient with prostate cancer diagnosis reported **"difficulty scheduling surgery"** -- 2-3 week pre-authorization delays
  - BBB: **"Communication with offices is poor, with difficulty getting call backs from doctors"**
  - Glassdoor: 3.1/5 overall; 2.4/5 compensation
  - Indeed: Patient Care Coordinator -- **"workload was always overwhelming"**
- **Why:** New CEO (late 2025) = change mandate. Patient reviews explicitly call out "clunky and unreliable" medical records. Duplicate billing, collections sent without original bills. Disconnected systems between scheduling, billing, insurance verification, and records.

### Mindfully Behavioral Health

  - Glassdoor: 3.1/5 overall; 41% would recommend
- **Why:** Documentation software employees openly despise. Management communication breakdown across 7-14 locations. 31 open positions. No standardized operational playbook. May exceed target size but massive ops pain.

### Dermatology & Advanced Skin Care

### Ecosystem Note: Industry Context
Cincinnati metro added **5,800 construction jobs** between June 2024-2025 (11% increase). **78% of firms** report difficulty filling hourly craft positions. **84% of remodelers** report subcontractor shortages. Every company on this list is under pressure to do more with less.

- **Website:** https://phillipssupply.com/
- **Size:** ~55-75 employees, $20.4M revenue (janitorial/sanitary distribution)
- **Founded:** 1947 (79 years, 3rd-generation family/woman-owned)
- **Key People:** **Pamela Phillips Rossmann (President/Owner, 50+ years in business)**; Thomas Margraf (GM)
- **Tech Stack:** Government vendor (SAM.gov). FMCSA registered. No modern ERP visible.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Indeed: **"Warehouse is small and cramped, an accident waiting to happen"**
  - Indeed: **"Expectations are high"** but **"higher ups do not lead by example"**
  - Also positive: Owners are **"absolutely amazing people"**
- **Why:** Pamela Rossmann cares deeply but systems aren't keeping up. $20M+ across healthcare, government, education customers with government compliance requirements that strain manual systems.

  - Owner took over after founder's unexpected passing — business continuity was chaotic, documentation poor

  - Furniture installation team adds project management complexity
  - Competes against Amazon Business — operational efficiency is existential

### FRY Fastening Systems ★ NEW
- **Website:** https://www.frysys.com
- **Size:** ~23 employees across 3 distribution centers
- **Founded:** 1986
- **Key People:** Greg Burkhart (President/CEO); Phil Burkhart (COO)

  - THREE separate business lines: product sales, warranty/repair service, and tool rental — each with completely different workflows
  - Three distribution centers = multi-location inventory management
  - Fry's Nail Gun Depot is a separate e-commerce brand/channel — likely running on different system than B2B
  - Tool rental requires asset tracking, maintenance scheduling, rental billing
  - Warranty service requires repair tracking, parts inventory, manufacturer claims processing
- **Why:** Greg Burkhart running three businesses in one across three locations with ~23 people. Data and workflow complexity is massive for this size. Connecting tools and automating handoffs could yield enormous efficiency gains.

### Chrisco Restaurant Design & Supply ★ NEW
- **Website:** https://chriscodesign.com
- **Size:** 2-4 employees, $5-10M revenue
- **Founded:** ~2002
- **Key People:** Chris Ferraro (Owner); Eleni Ferraro (Co-Owner); Trent Heimann (team member)
- **Tech Stack:** Basic website. No e-commerce or online catalog. Phone/email only.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - $5-10M in revenue with 2-4 people — extraordinary throughput per person
  - Design services require project management (drawings, approvals, equipment selection, ordering, installation scheduling)
  - New AND used equipment = two different sourcing and pricing models
  - 4-city service region (Cincinnati, Dayton, Louisville, Lexington) with 2-4 people
- **Why:** Chris and Eleni ARE the operations team. Every process lives in their heads. If Chris gets sick, the business stops. Systematizing quoting, project management, and order tracking would be transformative even if simple.

### Supplier/Distributor Vertical-Wide Themes (updated)

1. **"WooCommerce/Shopify for B2B"** — Asad Wholesale, Tri-State Wholesale, Queen City Restaurant Supply all use consumer e-commerce platforms stretched for wholesale workflows. No customer-specific pricing, net terms, or PO support.
2. **"Walk-in Counter + Delivery"** dual workflow — Sunset Janitorial, Murphy Supply, Tri-State, Phillips Supply, Edgeco, Queen City. Each requires different order processing, rarely sharing a system.
3. **"Family Succession and Ownership Transitions"** — Murphy (3rd gen), Queen City (Foust→Carr), Supply Post (post-founder death), Cincinnati Fastener (2nd gen), Keidel (Winsupply acquisition). Each creates a modernization opportunity.
4. **"Phone/Fax Ordering Persists"** — Asad Wholesale explicitly accepts fax. Sunset, Edgeco, Chrisco appear phone/email-only. Low-hanging fruit for automation.
5. **"The Office Manager Is the Real Backbone"** — Phillips Supply's Joseph Warakomski, Stigler's Beth Glassmeyer and Tricia Rohling, Avsten's Erin Wood. These are the entry points who feel the pain daily.
6. **"Extreme Revenue-to-Staff Ratios"** — Chrisco ($5-10M with 2-4 people), Supply Post (40K SKUs with 9), JB Doppes (157 years of product diversity with 16 people). When everything runs through one or two people's heads, the business is one illness away from crisis.

### Industry Context
**43% of small businesses** don't track inventory or use manual processes, losing up to **11% of annual revenue** to inefficiencies. Typical progression: QuickBooks year 1-3, Excel year 3-5, "patchwork of disconnected systems held together by manual processes" after year 5.

# BLUE COLLAR SERVICES

## Priority 1

### Scherzinger Pest Control
- **Website:** https://stopzbugs.com/
- **Size:** ~50 employees, $7.3M revenue, 3 metro locations (Cincinnati/NKY, Dayton, Columbus)
- **Founded:** 1934 (92 years, 4th generation)
- **Key People:** Steve Scherzinger (CEO, 3rd gen); Kurt Scherzinger (President, 4th gen); Eric Scherzinger (VP Procurement/Marketing, 4th gen); **Bill Brown (Area Operations Manager)**; Mike Wedding (Technical Director)
- **Tech Stack:** No confirmed FSM platform. Phone-heavy inbound model.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - BBB: **"My first appointment was a no-show and when I called, it was a scheduling error"**
  - BBB: **"Scherzinger had been billing me without providing service"**
  - BBB: Customer made **"4 calls between January 2024 to April"** and was **"assured a supervisor would call in 48 hours"** -- no callback
  - Customer: Had to **"sit through their on hold bull crap 7 or 8 times"**
  - Indeed: **"Field Support staff was merged with the call center and the work load became unmanageable"**
- **Why:** 90-year-old family business showing clear signs that back-office hasn't scaled. Technicians missing appointments, customers billed for services never rendered, call center merged with field support and "became unmanageable." Routing/scheduling doesn't talk to billing. Bill Brown (Ops Manager) lives in this pain.

  - Indeed: **"Managers mess with ur money and every check will be wrong"**

  - Indeed: **"There was zero communication internally"**
- **Why:** 40+ trucks across 4 cities with PHONE-CALL dispatch. Payroll wrong "every check." Crews understaffed because nobody tracks job-to-crew ratios. Elaine Morris (budgets + operations) and Jason (Ops Manager) feel this most.

### Cross-Cutting Themes
1. **"Phone Number Dispatch"** -- Leaders Moving tells employees to call a phone number the night before. Scherzinger has customers on hold 7-8 times. Telephone-era tools for logistics operations.
2. **"Billing for Phantom Service"** -- Scherzinger billed for services never delivered. Eads couldn't track material orders vs jobs. Leaders has payroll errors every check. When billing, service, and payroll aren't connected, money falls through cracks.
3. **"Multi-Location/Multi-System"** -- Scherzinger (3 cities), Leaders (4 cities), Fleet Care (8+ fleet portals), Eads (subcontractors) all coordinate across organizational boundaries.
4. **"Generational Transition"** -- Scherzinger (3rd→4th gen), Pest All (1st→2nd gen), Osterwisch (3rd gen), Wimberg (founder active). How to move from "the boss knows everything" to "the system knows everything."
5. **"Reluctant Operator"** -- Robinson (Brian), Quality Comfort (Ryan), Seasons Best (Jonathan), Advanced Mobile (Lawrence), G.I. Haul (Allan) are all founders exceptional at service work but now running complex operations they never trained for.

### Valley Termite & Pest Control
- **Website:** https://www.valleytermiteandpest.com/
- **Size:** ~15 employees, 60+ years in business
- **Key People:** Tami Burkel (Owner/President, NAPW VIP Woman of Year 2014); Mike Burkel (Technician Manager)
- **Tech Stack:** No identifiable FSM or scheduling software. Basic website. No online booking.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Multiple service types (pest control, termite treatment, animal removal, real estate inspections, mold inspections) each with different workflows and pricing models
  - 60-year family business transition — Tami took over from parents, inheriting legacy processes
  - Office hours limited to M-F 8-5, Sat 9-12 with no online scheduling
  - Real estate inspections + commercial pest control are recurring-revenue lines requiring different CRM approaches than residential
  - 5.0 Angi rating — maintaining quality at scale with manual processes is a time bomb
- **Why:** Tami is both owner AND office operations person. Cincinnati's only female-owned full-service pest management company. Running multi-service 60-year-old family business with family help and likely minimal tech.

### Schneller Knochelmann Plumbing Heating & Air
- **Website:** https://www.schnellerair.com/
- **Size:** 52 employees (12 office/sales, 40 field), 34 vehicles, 2 locations (Cincinnati + Covington KY)
- **Key People:** Lisa Knochelmann (Owner & VP, former accountant at CPA firm); Kris Knochelmann (co-owner, field ops)
- **Tech Stack:** No public evidence of ServiceTitan or Housecall Pro. Live agents until 9PM M-F + Saturdays.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Customer reviews mention scheduling callbacks and standby lists — manual or semi-manual scheduling
  - 34 vehicles dispatched across two states (different licensing/regulatory requirements)
  - Summer demand spikes cause "late hours" per Glassdoor
  - Customer complaints about appointment delays without timely updates — field-to-office communication gap
  - 12 office staff plus extended hours = heavy payroll commitment for phone/scheduling
- **Why:** Lisa's accounting background (former CPA firm) means she comes from structured environments and likely sees the operational gaps clearly. Co-purchased business in 2011, running 52 people and 34 trucks across two states. The heavy office staffing (12 people, 9PM hours) suggests process inefficiency.

### Jolly Plumbing Drains Heating & Air ★ HIGH PRIORITY
- **Website:** https://jollyplumbing.com/
- **Size:** 58 employees, 27 technicians, 3 locations, $9.4M revenue
- **Key People:** Brady Jolly (CEO/Owner); Scott Sharrock (Operations Director/COO — BBB customer contact)
- **Tech Stack:** **ServiceTitan** (confirmed) + **custom "Service Jack" reporting tool** built on top. After-hours AI scheduling with human follow-up.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - **Built custom reporting tool on top of ServiceTitan** — their primary platform doesn't fully meet their data/reporting needs. This is a direct buying signal for integration/optimization work.
  - Indeed reviews: **"highest employee turnover rate of any company I've ever worked for... BY FAR"**
  - Pressure to upsell creates field-vs-office tension
  - 5x revenue growth in a decade across 3 locations — systems that worked at $2M don't work at $10M
  - After-hours AI scheduling + human scheduler = hybrid approach potentially not fully integrated
- **Why:** Rare prospect where we KNOW the exact tech stack AND the specific gap. They use ServiceTitan but needed to build custom tools. That's an invitation for someone who can integrate, extend, and optimize existing tools. Scott Sharrock as Operations Director is the buyer. 2025 Residential Contractor of the Year.

### Delhi Pest Control
- **Website:** https://delhipest.com/
- **Size:** 4-5 employees, new ownership June 2024
- **Key People:** TJ Adams (Owner — took over June 2024)
- **Tech Stack:** Likely just QuickBooks and phone. No online scheduling visible. Limited hours M-F 8-5, Sat 9-12.

  - Brand new owner inheriting 40+ year old business and its legacy processes
  - 5 employees with 165 years combined experience — knowledge in people's heads, not systems
  - 5.0 Google rating with limited reviews — reputation to protect while modernizing
  - TJ managing every customer interaction personally without online booking

### Ohio Building Services (OBS)
- **Website:** https://www.ohiobuildingservices.com/
- **Size:** ~32 employees, ~$5M revenue, founded 1978
- **Key People:** Lina Orr (President); Steven Statman (VP)
- **Tech Stack:** No identifiable scheduling or workforce management software. Wix website.

  - Indeed reviews: **"goes through managers way too fast"** — manager turnover is a strong ops/process failure signal
  - Employees working only 2 days/week wanting more hours — workforce scheduling and utilization issues
  - Diverse client types (offices, warehouses, schools, medical, fitness, retail) each have different protocols and compliance requirements
  - Owners answering every call directly — bottleneck that doesn't scale
  - No raises, no advancement from within — retention challenges strain thin management layer
- **Why:** Manager turnover problem screams disconnected operations. When managers can't succeed, they often lack the tools. Commercial cleaning across dozens of client sites with different schedules, protocols, and part-time crews is inherently complex. Lina and Steve are drowning in operational details.

### Cougar Electric
- **Website:** https://www.cougarelec.com/
- **Size:** 13+ licensed electricians, commercial/industrial, women-owned
- **Key People:** Chris Elam (President); Mike Tepker (Operations Manager)

  - Commercial/industrial focus means complex project scheduling, material ordering, permit tracking, and crew management
  - 15,000+ completed jobs with spotless safety record — safety compliance documentation is a massive operational burden
  - BBB "not rated" despite being established since 2005 — limited digital presence suggests limited digital operations
  - Multi-generational family business with 13+ electricians — growth may have outpaced admin infrastructure
- **Why:** Women-owned commercial electrical contractor. Safety/compliance documentation alone is a significant ops burden. Tight-knit family nature means operations knowledge lives in people, not systems.

### iShine Cincy
- **Website:** https://ishinecincy.com/
- **Size:** 1-10 employees, commercial pressure washing + general contracting
- **Key People:** Jacob Gilbert (Owner/Operator, Lakota West HS alumnus)
- **Tech Stack:** WordPress. No CRM or scheduling visible. BBB accredited A+ since 2020.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Running TWO companies (iShine pressure washing + Cincinnati Affordable Contracting since Dec 2023) with shared resources
  - 1,500+ customers in under 6 years — rapid growth for small crew
  - Commercial focus (apartments, hotels, parking garages) means recurring contracts and multi-site coordination
  - Family-owned with no franchise support — building all systems from scratch
- **Why:** Young entrepreneur juggling two companies with a small team. Split between pressure washing and general contracting means two sets of books, two scheduling systems, shared crews. Growing fast enough to need systems but hasn't had time to build them.

### Blue Collar Vertical-Wide Themes (updated)

1. **"Phone Number Dispatch"** -- Leaders Moving tells employees to call a phone number the night before. Scherzinger has customers on hold 7-8 times. Telephone-era tools for logistics operations.
2. **"Billing for Phantom Service"** -- Scherzinger billed for services never delivered. Eads couldn't track material orders vs jobs. Leaders has payroll errors every check. When billing, service, and payroll aren't connected, money falls through cracks.
3. **"Multi-Location/Multi-System"** -- Scherzinger (3 cities), Leaders (4 cities), Fleet Care (8+ fleet portals), Eads (subcontractors), Jolly (3 locations + ServiceTitan + custom tools), Schneller (2 states) all coordinate across organizational boundaries.
4. **"Generational Transition"** -- Scherzinger (3rd→4th gen), Pest All (1st→2nd gen), Osterwisch (3rd gen), Wimberg (founder active), Valley Termite (parents→Tami), Delhi (new owner 2024). How to move from "the boss knows everything" to "the system knows everything."
5. **"Reluctant Operator"** -- Robinson (Brian), Quality Comfort (Ryan), Seasons Best (Jonathan), Advanced Mobile (Lawrence), G.I. Haul (Allan), iShine (Jacob) are all founders exceptional at service work but now running complex operations they never trained for.
6. **"Known Stack with Known Gaps"** -- Jolly Plumbing is the standout: ServiceTitan user who built custom reporting on top because the off-the-shelf solution isn't enough. This is the dream pitch for integration/optimization work.

---

# NEXT STEPS

1. **Start with Priority 1 prospects across all verticals** — these have the strongest, most specific pain signals
2. **For each Priority 1 prospect, draft a personalized email** using the pain signal as the opening observation
3. **Community Shares is a strategic play** — if you can help them, you get introduced to 45 progressive nonprofits
4. **SpliceNet Consulting** (law firm IT) — explore whether they're a referral partner or competitor
5. **Track outreach in the CSV** — update Status column as you go
6. **Contact scraping complete** — All 9 verticals now have email/phone/confidence data. 39 CONFIRMED, 63 INFERRED (call to verify before sending), 24 GENERIC, 5 empty (no data found)
7. **Continue growing toward 500** — Currently at 384 prospects across 13 verticals in Cincinnati. Phase C gap-filling complete for Law (+12), Nonprofit (+14), Accounting (+9), Real Estate (+9). Need ~116 more to reach 500.

# BLUE COLLAR SERVICES — BATCH 1 EXPANSION (Landscaping, Tree Service, Pool Service)
### Researched 2026-02-12

## Priority 1

### Seiler's Landscaping
- **Website:** https://www.seilerslandscaping.com/
- **Size:** ~35 employees, $4M revenue (targeting $10M by 2030)
- **Founded:** 1977 by Jim Seiler; Will Seiler (son) purchased Jan 1, 2020
- **Key People:** Will Seiler (Owner, lives in Boulder CO); Dave Parrish (General Manager, runs daily Cincinnati ops); Stacy Flannery (Controller); Greg Kuykendall (Construction Mgr); Elliott Rubin (Maintenance Mgr); Darren Shick, Monica Riordan, Anna Kersker (Sales/Design)
- **Tech Stack:** Aspire (FSM), CompanyCam, Jeffrey Scott's Leaders Edge rolling budget, Squarespace website, MailChimp, Google Analytics, Facebook Pixel
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Owner lives in Boulder, CO — **manages Cincinnati operations remotely, visiting "about three or four days" per month.** Dave Parrish is the de facto operator.
  - Revenue tripled from **$1.5M to $4M** in four years post-acquisition. Systems built at $1.5M are being stretched to handle $4M.
  - **6 open positions** at a 35-person company = attempting to fill **17% of workforce**. Open roles include Project Manager and Office/Admin — signals management layer is insufficient.
  - Will Seiler aims to **"begin acquiring other local service companies"** — M&A without integration infrastructure is an operational time bomb.
  - Purchased the company **January 1, 2020** — weeks before COVID lockdowns. Foundational systems were built under crisis conditions.
  - Aspire Software friction: Will noted **"The trick is choosing the right data to share"** — common Aspire UX complaint about information overload.
  - Shifting from **65% design/build, 35% maintenance to 50/50** — maintenance expansion requires fundamentally different ops (recurring routes, seasonal scheduling, quality audits).
- **Why:** This is the highest-value landscaping prospect on the list. Will Seiler is an engaged, growth-minded owner who already invests in tools (Aspire, CompanyCam, Leaders Edge peer group) — but he's 1,500 miles away trying to manage by monthly data recaps. The gap between his ambitions ($10M, acquisitions, service mix shift) and his current infrastructure ($4M, remote oversight, 17% open headcount) is enormous. Dave Parrish (GM) is the Backbone keeping it all running on-site. The pitch: "The systems that got you from $1.5M to $4M — are those the same systems that get you to $10M while you're managing from Boulder?"

Every one of these failures (misdiagnoses, wrong dispatches, no-shows, lost records) is directly addressable with basic operational systems. Don Marcum is a Reluctant Operator who has run this business for 59 years on personal knowledge and relationships, but the organization has outgrown those methods.

  - BBB complaint: **"The project management on the job was horrendous."**
  - BBB complaint: **"The project manager even told me someone on his crew told him to just lie to me about something being completed because 'I would never notice.'"**
  - BBB complaint: **"His scheduling was awful. Three times we scheduled they just did not show up at all — I had to reach out hours or a day after the scheduled date and ask why they weren't here."**
  - Indeed: **"No room for growth, no management, lots of nepotism within the company."**
  - Indeed: **"Pay is far below identical jobs in the same industry."**
- **Why:** The scheduling no-shows and crew lying about completed work are the most visceral pain signals in the restoration category. Three no-shows in a single customer engagement, crew members being told to just lie about work completion — these are not abstract process failures, they are concrete, documented breakdowns in field-to-office communication. A 27-year-old company with ~20 employees running 24/7 emergency response across Cincinnati, NKY, SE Indiana, and Dayton without any visible dispatch or project management software. Christine Dattilo (Office Manager) is the Backbone. BBB accredited. Cleves OH.

### Pest All Exterminating (UPGRADED from 2-MED to 1-HIGH)

Rohde & Son Funeral Home, Mount Lookout. Survived by wife Jeanne, son Peter Jr. (Tracy), daughter Lorie Rumsey (Joe), and 5 grandchildren.
- **Impact:** Peter Jr. is now running a 58-year-old business alone that was built on his father's personal relationships and institutional memory. The founder was reportedly still involved until recently ("allowing his father to step back"). Multiple employees with 20+ year tenure — all processes live in their heads. After losing the founder, this institutional knowledge risk is acute.
- **Additional Findings:** Route technician Adam McPherson runs "Critter Combat LLC" as a side business (wildlife removal) — may indicate he feels undercompensated or sees uncaptured opportunity. Doug Smith identified as Sales Inspector. Fax number still prominently listed on website. BBB A+ since 1991. Norwood Chamber member.
- **Why Upgraded:** The founder's death less than a year ago is the single most significant pain signal. The window of receptivity to operational change is open right now — Peter Jr. must operationalize what was informal and relationship-based.

### Delhi Pest Control (UPGRADED from 3-MED to 2-MED)

- **Additional Findings:** Business reincorporated as "Project Bug, LLC" on 3/28/2024. BBB accreditation obtained 4/7/2025 (10 months after purchase). 4.9/5 on Birdeye with 183 reviews. Technicians named in reviews: Barry, Jim, Tom, Bob. Previously owned by Bob & Diana Grinkemeyer since 1982. Bob served on the County Advisory Board.
- **Why Upgraded:** New ownership (8 months ago) + active hiring with benefits = growth-mode company in the optimal receptivity window. TJ hasn't yet calcified into "the way we've always done it" and is investing seriously.

  - Broad service mix (plumbing, landscaping, construction, handyman) = massive scheduling complexity.

  - Nextdoor Neighborhood Favorite 2022-2023 — demand is strong, ops are the bottleneck.
- **Why:** The "trouble with follow up" quote is the most direct customer statement of operational pain. A company with strong demand (Nextdoor Favorite) and a broad service mix but no scheduling technology. The CEO title (unusual for a handyman company) signals professionalization aspirations that outpace current systems. Terrace Park/Cincinnati OH.

- **Size:** 3-10 employees, handyman + remodeling
- **Founded:** ~1990 (35+ years)

The quality of work is good when it gets done, which makes the operational failures even more frustrating for customers. BBB accredited since 2016. Cincinnati OH.

- **Tech Stack:** GPS-guided heavy equipment in the field (advanced), but NO office/operations software. No PM. No scheduling. No dispatch. No fleet management despite DOT fleet. Single generic inbox.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Indeed Equipment Operator (2.5/5), Dump Truck Driver (1.5/5), Superintendent (2.0/5):
  - **"A typical day felt disorganized and exhausting."**
  - **"There is no communication from the higher ups to the guys actually doing the work."**
  - **"Absolutely no communication with supervisors at all."**
  - **"Equipment is worn down and it's hard to get the mechanics to fix anything."**
  - **"Drivers almost killed themselves because of brake failure due to not servicing the brakes."**
  - **"Continuously employs outside managers who have not the slightest idea what is actually making the company money."**
- **Why:** Grew too fast for its systems. GPS-guided equipment in the field but zero communication, scheduling, or dispatch software in the office. The Indeed reviews are devastating — employees describe daily chaos, dangerous equipment, and management that has no field credibility. Not BBB accredited. Blue Ash, OH.

- **Gaebel Masonry** — Too small (2-10 employees). Rural base (Somerville, OH — 40 miles from downtown). Master craftsman-led but may not justify consulting engagement.

**Excavation:**

## MEDICAL/DENTAL — BATCH 7 EXPANSION: Veterinary Clinics

**Added 2026-02-12 | +14 new prospects | Running total: 228/500**

### Industry Context

Veterinary clinics are ideal Ops for Shops prospects because the owner-DVMs want to practice medicine, not manage operations. Most independent clinics have 8-25 staff (DVMs + techs + front desk) and run on a patchwork of practice management software, phone-based scheduling, and manual processes. Corporate consolidation (Mars/VCA, NVA, Pathway, Thrive, PetVet, Heartland, Mission) has acquired thousands of practices, but Cincinnati still has a strong independent clinic base. Key pain signals: phone-only scheduling overwhelming front desk, hour-long wait times, billing friction, staff burnout/turnover, fragmented client communication tools (PetDesk bolted on top of legacy systems), and owner-DVMs who never planned to be business managers. The "Backbone" persona is the Practice Manager/Office Manager; the "Reluctant Operator" is the owner-DVM.

#### Priority 1

##### Montgomery Animal Hospital
- **Website:** https://montgomeryanimalhospital.com/
- **Size:** 3 DVMs + 12-18 total staff, AAHA accredited
- **Founded:** 1940 (84 years, 4th independent owner)
- **Key People:** Dr. Diane Krumanaker (Owner, OSU 2021), Connor (Practice Manager & RVT, 5+ years — the Backbone), CSRs: Margot, Christina, Anna, Jenny
- **Email:** info@montgomeryanimalhospital.com (GENERIC)
- **Tech Stack:** GeniusVets website. No online booking — phone only. No client portal. CareCredit.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Indeed employee: **"Management is terrible, the entire hospital is unorganized"**
  - Recent ownership transition (~2023-2024) = systems in flux
  - No online booking = 4 CSRs buried in phone calls
- **Why:** A recently acquired practice with a young owner-DVM who wants to focus on medicine. The Indeed review citing disorganization + ownership transition = a practice actively looking for better systems. Connor (Practice Manager) is the ideal first contact — he has institutional knowledge and would immediately see the value in workflow improvements.

##### Glenway Animal Hospital
- **Website:** https://www.glenwayanimalhospital.com/
- **Size:** 2 DVMs + 10-20 total staff, AAHA accredited
- **Founded:** 1995 (Drs. Brian & Diana Cron purchased from Dr. Fred Leininger)
- **Key People:** Dr. Brian Cron (Owner), Dr. Diana Cron (Owner), Michele Mescher (Hospital Administrator & RVT — since July 1996, 30 years! — the Backbone), Becky Hafertepen (CSR), Colleen Steinmetz (CSR since 2012)

  - Yelp: **"They're always at least an hour behind"**
  - **"Expected to wait 2 weeks to bring a dog in with an ear infection"**
  - **"Desk people are rude"** — front-desk overwhelm, not attitude
  - Using both PetDesk AND PetsApp = fragmented client communications
- **Why:** A husband-wife practice with a 30-year Hospital Administrator (Michele Mescher) who is the operational heart. Hour-behind scheduling, 2-week booking delays, and front-desk friction despite adopting PetDesk AND PetsApp — they're throwing tools at the problem without a strategy. Michele is the ideal first contact.

- **Foot & Ankle Specialists** — PE-owned (NMS Capital roll-up)
- **Ohio Foot & Ankle Specialists** — Too large (35+ locations)
- **Foot Specialists of Greater Cincinnati** — Closed permanently Nov 2025

# SUPPLIERS — EXPANDED (Batches 10-11)

**Added 2026-02-12 | +18 new prospects | Running total: 272/500**

## Industry Context — New Sub-segments

The original Suppliers vertical focused on plumbing/HVAC, janitorial, industrial, and building material distributors. Batches 10-11 expand into four new sub-segments: **auto parts & recycling**, **food service supply**, **safety/PPE & packaging**, and **electrical/HVAC distribution**.

**Auto parts recyclers** are operationally fascinating — managing acres of vehicles with hundreds of thousands of SKUs, often with no digital inventory system. The industry is consolidating (LKQ, KOI, Smyth/Fisher), but Cincinnati has a cluster of multi-generational independents still running on phone orders, paper tickets, and eBay side hustles.

**Food service suppliers** face brutal competition from Sysco, US Foods, and Gordon Food Service. Independents survive on relationships and niche specialization (ethnic markets, institutional, used equipment), but their back offices often run on "very old software" or no software at all. Employee turnover is a reliable pain signal — warehouse and delivery work is physically demanding, and companies that underpay or mismanage see it in their Indeed reviews.

**Safety/PPE distributors** are a hidden gem. Companies like First Star Safety serve government contracts (MBE/SBE certified) that require operational rigor they may not yet have. Packaging distributors managing multi-warehouse operations face classic inventory coordination challenges.

**Electrical/HVAC distribution** is heavily consolidated nationally (Graybar, CES, Wesco, Rexel), but Cincinnati still has family-owned independents. The strongest signal: in 2026, a wholesale distributor with no e-commerce is losing business daily. Several prospects here are 50-90 years old and still phone-order-only.

## Priority 1

### Stricker Auto Parts
- **Website:** https://strickerautoparts.com/
- **Size:** ~36 employees, 68-acre facility, 185K sq ft warehouse, 300K+ SKUs
- **Founded:** 1955 (71 years). Family-owned, three generations (Stricker family).
- **Key People:** Arthur Stricker (President), John Stricker (owner/operator), Cathy Stricker (co-owner)
- **Tech Stack:** Basic WordPress site. No online ordering (sells on eBay as side channel). Cash/check only — no credit card processing. No visible ERP or inventory system.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Does NOT accept credit cards or returns: *"They don't accept returns or credit cards."* (Yelp/Birdeye)
  - Parts quality disputes: *"Paid $2,100 for a lift gate assembly described as in excellent condition, but a wiring harness, two object sensors were damaged, and interior panels were missing."* (Birdeye)
  - Inconsistent service: *"Drove much farther to avoid dealing with [specific staff member]"* (Google) — process depends on which person you get
  - Indeed wages $12.55-$15.49/hr — retention pressure
- **Why:** A 36-person operation managing 300K+ SKUs across 68 acres with no credit card processing, no online ordering, and no returns policy is almost certainly running on paper and tribal knowledge. The no-credit-card policy alone is a red flag for back-office modernization needs.

  - Communication and delay complaints across multiple platforms
  - 3.9/5 with 262 reviews — notably lower than competitors
- **Why:** Pricing disputes, prepayment problems, and communication breakdowns point to a lack of standardized quoting, order tracking, and customer communication tools. The two-competing-websites situation confirms there's no coherent digital strategy.

- **Why:** A 57-year-old business that just went through a generational ownership change is in a prime modernization window. Running two locations with dual revenue streams without visible digital tools means the new owners are juggling spreadsheets across sites. Generational transitions are the single best buying window.

# PROPERTY MANAGEMENT — EXPANDED (Batch 12)

**Added 2026-02-12 | +11 new prospects | Running total: 283/500**

## Industry Context — HOA, Commercial PM, Student Housing

The original Property Management vertical focused on residential rental PM companies. Batch 12 expands into three sub-segments: **HOA/community association management**, **commercial property management**, and **student housing management**.

**HOA management** in Cincinnati is a consolidation story — Cedar Management Group (200-500 employees) and Towne Properties (500-1,000) dominate, while Elite Management merged into Cedar in Oct 2025. The independents that remain are either legacy firms with 40+ year histories and dated infrastructure, or fast-growing startups scaling across metro areas without standardized processes. The recurring pain signal is **homeowner communication failures** — portal access issues, unreturned calls, missed maintenance for months or years.

**Commercial PM** independents are rarer, as CBRE/JLL/Cushman dominate. The survivors tend to be multi-generational family firms with diverse portfolios (retail + office + medical + industrial) creating operational complexity that outpaces their basic tools. The standout signal: firms managing 1M+ sq ft with no enterprise PM software.

**Student housing** operators face intense seasonal cycles — annual lease-ups, mass move-in/move-out, high maintenance volume — that expose process gaps relentlessly. Small operators near UC, Xavier, and Miami University often run on relationships and spreadsheets.

## Priority 1

### Management Plus Realty Services
- **Website:** https://www.managementplusrealtyservice.com/
- **Size:** ~15 employees. Only Cincinnati-native firm with AAMC designation from Community Associations Institute.
- **Founded:** 1984 (40+ years). Women-owned.
- **Key People:** Kelly Smith (Owner & Community Association Manager)
- **Tech Stack:** WordPress website. No confirmed HOA management software. Portal login complaints suggest outdated/broken system.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - BBB: *"I have been blown off by Management Plus since I moved into my neighborhood in 2021."*
  - Portal/access: *"I could not log in for two months and could not get in touch with anyone over the phone or through email."* (Nov 2024)
  - Maintenance: *"I notified Management Plus of water leaks I've been having over 2 years ago and they have failed to fix any of the leaks."*
  - Counter-positive: *"worked with Management Plus essentially every week for over 20 years...they consistently strive to do what is best for the communities"*
- **Why:** 40-year firm with clear tech gaps causing communication breakdowns. Portal access failures and phone/email unresponsiveness suggest outdated systems. Women-owned small business is an ideal client profile. The AAMC designation shows professional aspiration that their technology hasn't kept up with.

  - No Glassdoor/Indeed/BBB — too small for public reviews

- **Why:** 9 people managing 160+ industrial properties is an extreme ratio that practically guarantees operational bottlenecks. Young founders (2017) would be open to technology solutions. The fastest-growing company in this batch — growth is outpacing their ability to manage manually.

# RESTAURANTS/HOSPITALITY (Batches 13-15) — NEW VERTICAL

**Added 2026-02-12 | +15 new prospects (Batch 13) | Running total: 298/500**

## Industry Context

Cincinnati's restaurant scene is vibrant but operationally brutal. The city has a deep bench of multi-unit operators, chef-driven restaurant groups, and catering companies — but beneath the Instagram-worthy food photos, the back-of-house operations are often held together by duct tape and institutional memory.

**Three pain patterns dominate this vertical:**

1. **Scheduling chaos** is epidemic. Employee reviews across every sub-segment cite inconsistent scheduling, last-minute changes, punitive hour adjustments, and no-call/no-show management. Multi-unit operators compound this — scheduling across 4-7 locations with different concepts and different staffing models is nearly impossible without systems.

2. **Post-merger/expansion growing pains.** Cincinnati has seen a wave of restaurant group consolidation (DelightMore merging two catering companies, Strong's expanding from 1 to 5 locations across 3 states, E+O Kitchen adding a 3rd location despite documented financial issues). Each expansion strains processes that were designed for a single location.

3. **Franchise operator gaps.** National brands mandate POS and ordering systems but leave scheduling, payroll, inventory, and multi-unit coordination to the franchisee. A local operator running 4-6 franchise locations has the operational complexity of a small business but none of the corporate support for back-office systems.

The Cincinnati restaurant market is also experiencing a contraction cycle — Pesola Hospitality closed 3 concepts (Jan 2025), Catch-a-Fire closed 3 of 4 locations (Jan 2026), A Tavola OTR closed (Dec 2025). Operators who survive will be those who tighten operations. This is a buying moment.

## Priority 1

### Cafeo Hospitality Group (incl. Bell Event Centre)
- **Website:** https://cafeohospitality.com/
- **Size:** ~50-80 employees across 7 active concepts in 4 cities
- **Concepts:** Incline Public House, Jefferson Social, Press on Monmouth, Press at the Atrium, The Green Line Kitchen & Cocktails, Billy Yanks (Hamilton), Bell Event Centre, Incline Smoke Shack

  - Indeed (Incline Public House): "Long hours" challenge

  - Recently closed Somm Wine Bar+Kitchen (March 2025) — operational pressure
  - 7 diverse concepts across Cincinnati, Newport KY, Fort Thomas KY, and Hamilton OH — coordination nightmare
- **Why:** Family-founded group with 7 diverse concepts across 4 cities. The mix of event venue, full-service restaurants, and casual concepts means scheduling across very different staffing models. Recently closing a concept signals they're looking to tighten operations. Bell Event Centre's "teenage workforce" characterization implies high turnover and no SOPs.

# AUTO SERVICES (Batches 16-17) — NEW VERTICAL

**Added 2026-02-12 | +16 new prospects | Running total: 314/500**

## Industry Context

Cincinnati's independent auto service landscape mirrors the national trend: consolidation is relentless (Caliber, Gerber, Service King in collision; Mister Car Wash, WhiteWater Express in car wash; Tire Discounters with 190+ locations locally), but a stubborn core of family-owned shops survives on relationships and craftsmanship. These shops are operationally frozen in time.

**Four pain patterns define this vertical:**

1. **Multi-location growing pains.** The most acute pain is in shops that recently expanded from 1 to 2-3+ locations. Overbeck (1→3 shops), Smith Family Collision (acquired 3 shops in 3 years), Xpress Pro (transitioning 26 Car-X locations to independent brand), and Cincinnati Transmission (added 2nd location 2019) are all experiencing the classic "what worked at one location breaks at two" phenomenon — scheduling, parts ordering, customer communication, and quality consistency all degrade.

2. **Fleet service complexity.** Fleet customers (Midwest Fleet Services, Fleet Care, M&G Body Shop) demand faster turnaround, professional invoicing, warranty tracking, and fleet-level reporting that manual shops can't deliver. The fleet segment is growing but the shops serving it are still running on paper.

3. **Towing/dispatch chaos.** Schaffer's Towing (Gmail for quotes, 40+ vehicle fleet) and Bill's Towing (Indeed reviews citing workplace hostility) represent towing companies where dispatch, quoting, and fleet management are done by gut feel. A 90-year-old towing company using Gmail for quotes is the towing equivalent of Bernens Pharmacy using @fuse.net.

4. **Owner-operator bottleneck.** Across the vertical, the owner IS the process. Rick Lamping at Cincinnati Transmission, Mike Yeager at Northgate Transmissions, Dale Donovan at Donovan's — they're personally involved in every job, every estimate, every decision. When they take a sick day, the shop stops.

## Priority 1

### Overbeck Auto Services
- **Website:** https://overbeckauto.com/
- **Size:** ~15-25 employees across 3 locations
- **Founded:** 1971 (54 years). Steve Overbeck started after returning from Navy/Vietnam. Now run by son Matt (2nd gen).
- **Locations:** Madisonville, Springdale, Amelia
- **Key People:** Matt Overbeck (Owner/Operator), Steve & Ann Overbeck (founders)
- **Tech Stack:** Modern WordPress website. Online scheduling. Unknown shop management software.
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Actively hiring Automotive Technicians on Glassdoor and Indeed — staffing pressure across 3 locations
  - Customer reported receiving unsolicited $6,000 repair proposal for a sunroof diagnostic and oil change — service advisor process/communication issues
  - Personnel calling in sick causing longer appointment waits
  - Service Advisor pay $17.32/hr — turnover risk
- **Why:** Three-location family shop growing faster than its processes. The jump from 1 to 3 locations creates scheduling, parts ordering, and customer communication complexity that back-office optimization directly addresses.

### Smith Family Collision Centers
- **Website:** https://anderson-collision.com/ / https://jernyernst.com/ / https://boruskecollision.com/
- **Size:** ~15-30 employees across 3 acquired collision shops
- **Founded:** Boruske Brothers (1960s, acquired June 2018), Anderson Collision (1950 as Bert's Body Works, acquired Dec 2019), Jerry Ernst (1972, acquired Oct 2021)

- **Pain Signals:**
  - Acquired 3 shops in 3 years — each with its own processes, its own customers, its own systems
  - Customer service depends on individual heroics: *"Michelle kept me updated at each stage"* and *"Scott was a huge advocate with insurance payments"* — not systematized
  - Running 3 separate websites for one ownership group = fragmented operations
  - DRP/insurance coordination across 3 locations is inherently complex
- **Why:** Textbook post-acquisition integration pain. Three independently-run collision shops now under one family ownership, each with different processes, different websites, different staff cultures. They need unified back-office operations — scheduling, insurance coordination, parts ordering, and customer communication.

### Xpress Pro Tire & Auto
- **Website:** https://www.xpresspro.com/
- **Size:** ~60-80+ employees across 26 locations (10 Cincinnati, 13 Indianapolis, 2 NKY, 1 Dayton)

  - Inconsistent quality across locations (CARFAX ratings range 4.5-4.8)
  - Just transitioned from Car-X franchise to independent brand — standardizing 26 locations without franchisor systems
- **Why:** A 26-location family business that just lost its franchisor's operations playbook when it went independent. Standardizing quality, scheduling, and customer communication across 26 locations in 4 markets without Car-X corporate is exactly the problem Ops for Shops solves. Borderline on size but the Cincinnati operations alone (10 locations) qualify.

- **Size:** 11-50 employees, 17 qualified technicians, 43,000 sq ft facility

### Schaffer's Towing & Recovery
- **Website:** https://schafferstowingrecovery.com/
- **Size:** ~12 employees, 29-40+ vehicles (light duty, flatbeds, heavy wreckers, 50-ton rotator)

  - *"Limited vacation (3 days), requiring use of personal phones with no reimbursement, and favoritism"*
  - Customer: *"$550 to drive 30 miles and pull a unit 10 feet in 15 minutes at 1am"*
- **Why:** A 90-year-old, 12-person towing company with a 40+ vehicle fleet using Gmail for quotes. Fleet dispatch, quoting, and scheduling workflows need systematization. The employee complaints about personal phone usage and no reimbursement suggest there's no company-provided dispatch system.
