# MANUFACTURING/FABRICATION (Batches 19-21) — NEW VERTICAL

**Added 2026-02-12 | +16 new prospects | Running total: 330/500**

## Industry Context

Cincinnati/Dayton is one of America's densest corridors for small manufacturers. The region's industrial heritage means there are hundreds of family-owned machine shops, metal fabricators, plastics molders, and printers — many founded 50-100+ years ago — that still operate on tribal knowledge, paper job tickets, and disconnected systems.

**Four pain patterns define this vertical:**

1. **ERP disconnection.** Even shops that have invested in ERP (like Tri-State Fabricators with JobBOSS2) often have quoting systems, quality systems, and scheduling tools that don't talk to each other. The Paperless Parts case study on Tri-State literally documents their "quoting system lacked integration with their ERP."

2. **Temp workforce chaos.** Manufacturing shops increasingly rely on temp agencies for production labor. Deimling/jeliho Plastics has temp workers *"scared to report issues because they fear being let go."* Spectra-Tech pays $500 hiring bonuses and $100/month attendance bonuses just to get people to show up. Managing a blended permanent/temp workforce without HR systems is a nightmare.

3. **Owner-operator bottleneck.** From All Craft Manufacturing (2 co-presidents who ARE the workforce) to Art Woodworking (Ralph Dickman running a 106-year-old shop with 25 open job postings), the owner is the single point of failure. These shops literally stop functioning when the owner takes a sick day.

4. **Certification vs. reality gap.** K&H Industries is ISO 9001:2015 certified but Indeed reviews say *"limited resources and direction for new employees."* HR Machine has an ISO 9001:2008 cert that may have lapsed. The gap between what's on paper (for customer audits) and what happens on the shop floor is where Ops for Shops lives.

**Full dossiers for this vertical are in:**
- `prospect-dossiers-specialty-manufacturing.md` (DF Electronics, Valley Metal Works, Spectra-Tech, K&H Industries, Powder Coating Specialty)
- `prospect-dossiers-printing-packaging-plastics-woodworking.md` (Deimling/jeliho, Art Woodworking, Queen City Printing, 3D Corrugated, Kahny Printing, A. Flottemesch)
- Machine shops/metal fab data inline from research agents (CMF, Tri-State Fabricators, Vulcan Tool, All Craft, HR Machine)

## Priority 1 (7 companies)

1. **Cincinnati Metal Fabricating** — 23 employees, 47 yrs. Indeed: *"poor sales and engineering management."* Hiring QC + sales roles. Owner works on shop floor = stretched thin.
2. **Tri-State Fabricators** — 25-50 employees, 42 yrs, 125K sq ft. Indeed 2.8/5. Admitted their quoting *"lacked integration with ERP system JobBOSS2."* Family-owned (Vogt family).
3. **DF Electronics** — 75 employees, $12M, 52 yrs. Indeed: *"The place is filthy"* and *"management is horrible."* Family-run (Fine family), no ISO.
4. **Valley Metal Works** — 34 employees, 80+ yrs. Indeed: *"3 owners constantly fighting against each other... this sinking ship."* Management 2.8/5.
5. **Spectra-Tech Manufacturing** — 60-84 employees, 28 yrs. Indeed: *"nepotism abounds"* and *"micro-managed daily tasks."* $500 hiring bonus + $100/month attendance bonus = retention crisis.
6. **Deimling/jeliho Plastics** — 50 employees, $23M, 50 yrs. Indeed: *"Can't keep good employees due to supervisors."* Temps *"scared to report issues."* 27 injection presses.
7. **Art Woodworking & Mfg** — 30 employees, 106 yrs. 25 open Indeed postings for 30-person shop = capacity crisis. No digital operations.

## Priority 2 (7 companies)

8. **Vulcan Tool Company** — 17 employees, 110 yrs. ISO + ITAR + JCP = heavy cert load for tiny team. New ownership 2020.
9. **All Craft Manufacturing** — 2-5 employees, 38 yrs. Co-presidents ARE the workforce. Basic HTML website.
10. **K&H Industries** — Est. 15-40 employees, 121 yrs. ISO certified but *"limited resources and direction for new employees."*
11. **Queen City Printing** — 5-10 employees, 100+ yrs. Has a dedicated cost accounting clerk in a sub-10-person shop = manual job costing.
12. **3D Corrugated** — 5-20 employees. 3rd ownership change in 13 years. New owner (March 2025) = greenfield ops opportunity.
13. **Kahny Printing** — 10-25 employees, 69 yrs. Fax number on website. Dual print + promo product lines on separate platforms.
14. **HR Machine** — 5-15 employees, 18 yrs. Outdated ISO 9001:2008 cert. Contact form only (no email, no phone). Women-owned.

## Priority 3 (2 companies)

15. **A. Flottemesch & Son** — 2-8 employees, 80 yrs. **AOL email address.** HTTP-only website. May be below 5-employee threshold.
16. **Powder Coating Specialty** — 1-10 employees. Well-run micro-shop. Owner wearing every hat. Small budget likely.

### Disqualified
- **Meta Manufacturing** — ~100 employees, exceeds cap
- **Faxon Machining** — Likely too large/corporate
- **Cincinnati Incorporated** — Large manufacturer of fab machines, not a job shop
- **O'Neal Manufacturing** — National subsidiary
- **Graphic Village** — Likely 100+ employees
- **PMC SMART Solutions** — Likely too large
- **Zumbiel Packaging** — Likely exceeds 80 employees
- **Pexco** — National corporation
- Various franchise printers (Minuteman, Allegra, PIP) — Not independent

# FITNESS/WELLNESS (Batch 22) — NEW VERTICAL

**Added 2026-02-12 | +12 new prospects | Running total: 342/500**

## Industry Context

The Cincinnati fitness market is dominated by national chains (Planet Fitness, LA Fitness, OrangeTheory) and franchise models, with a thin layer of independent operators in between. True mid-size independents (10-50 employees) are rare — most independent gyms are either large single-facility clubs or small boutique studios with fewer than 5 staff. The sweet spot for Ops for Shops is multi-location operators, legacy martial arts schools, and established CrossFit boxes where the owner-operator is stretched between coaching and business management. Pain signals cluster around scheduling chaos, manual billing, high turnover, and founders who can't step away from daily operations.

*Full dossiers: marketing/prospects/prospect-dossiers-fitness-gyms.md*

## Priority 1

### Body Alive Fitness
- **Website:** https://bodyalivefitness.com/
- **Size:** ~64 employees, 6 locations (4 Cincinnati + Denver + Arizona + online), ~$6M revenue
- **Founded:** ~2013
- **Key People:** Stephanie Bain (Owner), Paul Bain (Co-Owner)
- **Contact:** (513) 337-9830 / stephanie@bodyalivefitness.com (CONFIRMED)
- **Tech Stack:** Custom mobile app, WordPress site, ClassPass/Wellhub integrations, custom video streaming platform
- **Pain Signals:**
  - Glassdoor 2.0/5 (35 reviews, only 11% recommend): **"Can be disorganized and roles are constantly changing"**
  - **"Fired employees unexpectedly with no explanation"**
  - **"No system in place to hold the leadership accountable"**
  - **"The owner ruins it for everyone"** (Indeed)
  - BBB complaints about deceptive trial billing
- **Why:** Worst Glassdoor rating in the entire prospect database. 64 employees across 6 locations and 3 states with documented disorganization — the operational chaos is not subtle.

  - Glassdoor 4.2/5 but: **"overworked and underpaid"**, **"Different buildings with very different cultures"**, **"Lack of communication between departments"**
- **Why:** Multi-site + communication gaps + overwork = ops infrastructure gap.

### Professional Payroll Services Inc
- **Website:** https://cincypayroll.com/
- **Size:** ~10-20 employees
- **Founded:** ~1980 (40+ years)
- **Contact:** (513) 761-2860
- **Pain Signals:** BBB not accredited after 40+ years. Dedicated-processor model = single points of failure. Legacy processes almost certain.
- **Why:** Each client assigned to one person. When that person is sick/quits, everything breaks.

### MLA Companies
- **Website:** https://mlacompanies.com/
- **Size:** ~30 professionals
- **Founded:** 2006
- **Key People:** Seth Morgan (President & CEO)
- **Pain Signals:** 30 people serving 60+ clients across multiple states. Recent acquisition of LGI CFO. Multi-state operations.
- **Why:** Acquisition integration + multi-state + 60+ clients = classic scaling pain.

### Horizon Payroll Solutions
- **Website:** https://www.horizonpayrollsolutions.com/
- **Size:** ~10-20 employees
- **Key People:** Brad Johnson (President, former CPA)
- **Pain Signals:** ~1,000 clients in 40 states from ~15-person team. Recent senior ops hire. Dedicated Operations Assistant role exists.
- **Why:** 65 clients per person ratio across 40 states. Operational complexity is extreme.
